HORIZONTAL WELL
SCHNEIDER 7-33-28H-143-96 L
SWSW Section 33-143N-96W
Dunn County
Well File # 30560
Dear Elizabeth:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 25712, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement shall be located
approximately down the north-south axis (within the 500' drilling corridor per Commission policy) and no closer
than 200 feet to the north or south boundary within the 2560 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 28, 29, 32, &
33 T143N R96W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. Due to a drainage adjacent to the well site, a dike is required surrounding the entire
location. Conductor may only be set for the permitted wells on the pad. OXY USA INC must contact
NDIC Field Inspector Nicole Nelson at 701-290-1527 prior to location construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. The minimum legal coordinate from the well head at casing
point is: 593' west. Also, based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum legal coordinate from the
well head is: 10031' north.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
Elizabeth S. Bush-Ivie
January 23, 2015
Page 2
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

April 9, 2014
RE:
Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director

5D 7.5.8 : 20 August 2014, 13:19:56 UTC
OXY USA INC.
MIDCONTINENT BUSINESS UNIT
WILLISTON DIVISION
GAS CAPTURE PLAN
SCHNEIDER SWSW 33 PAD
SECTION 33-T143N-R96W
DUNN COUNTY, NORTH DAKOTA
SCHNEIDER 5-33-28H-143-96
SCHNEIDER 7-33-28H-143-96
JANUARY 15, 2014
Pad
The wells that will be located on the Schneider SWSW 33 Pad are shown in the table below.
Pipeline Notification
These wells will be connected to ONEOK's low pressure gathering system in Dunn County,
North Dakota. Oxy's acreage that comprises the spacing unit (SU) for the Schneider 5-33-28H-
143-96 and Schneider 7-33-28H-143-96 is dedicated to ONEOK. Under terms of the contract,
ONEOK is obligated to install the facilities that are required to connect these wells to its
gathering system. Oxy provides (on a monthly basis) to ONEOK a drilling, completion and
estimated first production date for all wells that are scheduled to be drilled in the foreseeable
future.
In addition, Oxy and ONEOK have conference calls, usually bi-weekly, to discuss
connection status of wells and changes to Oxy's drilling and completion schedules.
Gathering System
ONEOK's gathering system in this area is a dynamic system that has multiple compressor
stations with common suction lines. Gas produced from this pad will have a primary flow path
to ONEOK's Lodgepole compressor station and secondary flow paths to ONEOK's Killdeer and
Little Knife compressor stations. The actual flow of the gas will be based on compression
operating parameters and gathering system pressures. Gas gathered on this part of ONEOK's
gathering system is processed at ONEOK's Grassland Processing Plant located in Section 36,
T146N, R105W, McKenzie County, North Dakota.
In addition to ONEOK, Hiland has a low pressure gathering line less than 250' from the
Schneider SWSW 33 Pad location. Hiland's lines, along with ONEOK's, are shown on the
attached map.
The production facilities for the Schneider 5-33-28H-143-96 and Schneider 7-28-33H-143-96
will be located approximately 150' south of ONEOK's existing 12.75" outside diameter (OD)
low pressure gathering line. The connection to ONEOK will require approximately 150' of
either 4.50" or 6.625" OD low pressure gathering line and related facilities.
Existing Lines
3
At the terminus of the metering, associated piping at each well's production facilities and the
150' of 4.50" or 6.625" OD low pressure gathering line noted above, a connection will be made
to an existing 12.75" OD gathering line. This 12.75" OD gathering line traverses approximately
1.5 miles before connecting to a 16" OD gathering line. The gas then travels approximately 30.0
miles before being compressed at ONEOK's Lodgepole compressor station. This will be the
primary flow path of gas delivered to ONEOK from this pad.
As noted under "Gathering
System", above, the gas will have secondary flow paths due to the dynamics of ONEOK's
gathering system.
The table below shows the capacities and current flows of the primary
gathering lines connecting this well.
ONEOK's low pressure gathering system is near capacity in this area due to continuing
development of the fields in this area. It is projected that the system will have capacity when
these wells are ready for production due to decline on the existing wells gathered on this segment
of the system and ONEOK's continuing efforts to maximize flow on its gathering system(s).
ONEOK is in the process of adding compressors at its Lost Bridge compressor station in Section
14, T147N, R96W, Dunn County and installing a 16" OD low pressure gathering line that will
start in T145N, R94W, Dunn County (Dunn Center) and end at the inlet of the Lost Bridge
compressor station. Construction of these facilities will redirect gas that currently flows on the
primary and secondary flow paths of the Schneider SWSW 33 Pad to flow on the new facilities.
Although this does not directly increase the capacity of the primary and secondary flow paths of
the Schneider SWSW 33 Pad, it redirects gas that currently flows on the same pipelines to a
different compressor station, in essence reducing volumes transported on the flow paths for this
well.
ONEOK is also planning on constructing a new discharge line from its Lost Bridge
compressor station that will deliver some of the gas currently processed at ONEOK's Grasslands
Processing Plant to ONEOK's Garden Creek Processing Plant(s).
ONEOK has announced plans to construct the Bear Creek natural gas processing plant and
related natural gas and natural gas liquids infrastructure in Dunn County, North Dakota. The
Bear Creek natural gas processing plant and related facilities are expected to be operation during
the second quarter of 2016. In addition, ONEOK Demicks Lake natural gas processing plant,
located in McKenzie County, North Dakota, is expected to be operational during the third quarter
of 2016.
Flowback Strategy
4
After the fracture treatment, these wells will be flowed through a choke to test production tanks.
Choke size will depend on final shut in pressure post frac and well pressure prior to opening the
choke. The choke will be adjusted up or down based on flowing pressure, liquid rates and sand
returns, to prevent clogging manifold chokes. During flowback, the water chlorides and sand
content will be monitored. When the water chlorides are greater than 100,000 ppm and the
produced fluids contain no sand, the wells will be turned to production facilities. Since the
pipeline is already at the location of the pad and Oxy will have its production facilities
constructed before flowback starts, and gas sales should start as soon as the wells start flowing
through the production facilities, unless there are capacity issues on ONEOK's system at that
time. Based on current information, it is our belief the system can take this gas upon completion
of the wells.
The typical well on this pad will initially flow 445 barrels of oil and 200 thousand cubic feet of
gas per day based on Oxy's production type curve of this area. Based on current drilling and
completion plans, these wells will be completed in the same timeframe. For these two wells,
Oxy projects a peak oil rate of 890 barrels and a peak gas rate of 400 thousand cubic feet per day
from the pad. It is anticipated these wells will decline sharply after initial production as do the
majority of horizontal wells in the Williston Basin.
Current Flaring
The table below shows gas produced and sold by Oxy per Gas Production Report - Form 5B that
was filed by Oxy for October 2014 reporting period. The percent sold and percent flared are also
shown in the table.
Flaring
Wells on this pad will be connected to a pipeline prior to production and Oxy does not expect to
flare gas. Below are three alternatives that Oxy considered from a conceptual standpoint to
reduce the amount of gas flared. More generally, Oxy is continuing to review the possible
impact of implementing one or more of these alternatives as appropriate in our operations.
1) NGL Removal ­ On Lease
5
Captures highest value components in gas stream
Plants are expensive
Uneconomical to operate when volume declines
Residue gas is still flared
2) Power Generation ­ On Lease
Savings if current generation's fuel supply is diesel
Only a portion of gas is consumed operating the generator, remainder of gas will
be flared
Due to gas quality, high NGL content, preference is to purchase power from the
grid and not operate generation on site
3) Compressed Natural Gas ­ On lease
Well site compressors are required to fill CNG trailers
Large capital outlay for equipment and operating cost, includes trucking of
products, are expensive
No gas would be flared, but might be uneconomical to operate when gas volume
declines
6

SURFACE HOLE
843' FWL - 331' FSL
I, William H. Dolinar, Professional Land Surveyor, ND. RLS #6550, hereby certify that (in accordance with a request from Cody Dennison with Oxy USA, Inc., 3239 Highway
22, Dickinson, North Dakota 58601) I and/or personnel under my direction made a survey on the 13th day of June 2014, for the Surface Hole Location and Elevation of platted
well, being located within the SW1/4SW1/4 of Section 33, T143N, R96W of the 5th P.M., Dunn County, State of North Dakota.
Notes: All Azimuths are based on the South line of the Southwest Quarter of Section 33, T143N, R96W of the 5th P.M., being an Azimuth of 269°56'44" using GPS
observations, occupying a WHS control point (5/8" rebar) and having the Location and Elevation derived from an OPUS Solution and GEOID 09. Azimuths shown have been
rotated 1°43'25.54678" West from SPC Grid bearings to Geodetic North, based on convergence angle provided by a conversion using Corpscon.
Project elevations are held on the control point located 173°54'36", 4.48 Feet, from the Southwest Corner of Section 33, T143N, R96W of the 5th P.M. having a NAVD 88
elevation of 2421.44 feet.
Distances shown are Ground Distances using a combined scale factor of 1.000161758.
Location shown here on is not an "ASBUILT" location.
~SEAL~

Anti Collision Report Terminology
S.Minor, S.Major :Radii of the ellipse of uncertainty at the current location as seen in the along hole direction.
PHI :Angle between high-side vector and semi-minor axis
TVD Spread :Total TVD range of the ellipsoid of uncertainty at the current location
ES :Distance between the extremities of the primary and secondary uncertainty ellipsoids in the direction Cr-Cr
T.Face to Sec :Angle between the Hi-Side vector of the primary well at the current location and line of closest approach between the two wells
Separation factors calculated using Pedal Curve (Combined Uncertainty). Well path created using minimum curvature.
